        StackExchange.ready(function () {

            var location = 0;
            if ($("body").hasClass("questions-page")) {
                location = 1;;
            } else if ($("body").hasClass("question-page")) {
                location = 1;;
            } else if ($("body").hasClass("faq-page")) {
                location = 5;;
            } else if ($("body").hasClass("home-page")) {
                location = 3;;
            }

            $('#tell-me-more').click(function () {
                StackExchange.using("gps", function () {
                        StackExchange.gps.track("aboutpage.click", { aboutclick_location: "hero" }, true);
                    StackExchange.gps.track("hero.action", { hero_action_type: 'cta', location: location }, true);
                });
            });
            $('#herobox #close').click(function () {
                StackExchange.using("gps", function () {
                    StackExchange.gps.track("hero.action", { hero_action_type: "minimize", location: location }, true);
                });
                $.cookie("hero", "mini", { path: "/", expires: 365 });
                $.ajax({
                    url: "/hero-mini",
                    success: function (data) {
                        $("#herobox").fadeOut("fast", function () {
                            $("#herobox").replaceWith(data);
                            $("#herobox-mini").fadeIn("fast");
                        });
                    }
                });
                return false;
            });
        });

     <div id="question-header"> 
      <h1 itemprop="name"><a href="/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta" class="question-hyperlink">The Many Memes of Meta</a></h1> 
     </div> 
     <div id="mainbar"> 
      <div class="question" data-questionid="19478" id="question"> 
       <table> 
        <tbody>
         <tr> 
          <td class="votecell"> 
           <div class="vote"> 
            <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19478"> 
            <a class="vote-up-off" title="This question shows research effort; it is useful and clear">up vote</a> 
            <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">538</span> 
            <a class="vote-down-off" title="This question does not show any research effort; it is unclear or not useful">down vote</a> 
            <a class="star-off" href="#">favorite</a> 
            <div class="favoritecount">
             <b>350</b>
            </div> 
           </div> </td> 
          <td class="postcell"> 
           <div> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p>Catchphrases and concepts that spread from person to person are known as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_meme" rel="nofollow">memes</a>, which, courtesy the Internet, can now explode across the Earth like a highly contagious virus (hence "going viral"). As with their real-life counterparts, some infectious diseases are global (pandemic), while others are endemic to specific regions.</p> 
             <p>Stack Overflow, and now even more predominantly Meta Stack Overflow, have seen more than their fair share of these pathological social constructs spread through the user base. They are now ingrained units of our collective culture as SOpedians (a term which I hate, by the way).</p> 
             <p>Just as travelers' immune systems can be assaulted by new diseases in new places, new users are increasingly likely to be miffed by an ingrained meme and left sitting scratching their heads. I therefore propose that this space be used to document the memes endemic to Stack Exchange's culture.</p> 
             <p>Each meme should be listed separately and I hope that we as a community will be able to provide greater context to each one.</p> 
             <p><strong>Please actually explain each meme in a way understandable to those not already in the know.</strong></p> 
             <p><a href="/q/7931">Return to FAQ index</a></p> 
             <h2>On other Stack Exchange sites</h2>

                 <a href="/users/20654/oscarryz" title="3,112 reputation" class="comment-user">OscarRyz</a> 
                 <span class="comment-date" dir="ltr"><span title="2009-09-11 19:02:25Z" class="relativetime-clean">Sep 11 '09 at 19:02</span></span>

               <td class="comment-actions"> 
                <table> 
                 <tbody>

                 </tbody> 
                </table> </td> 
               <td class="comment-text"> 
                <div style="display: block;" class="comment-body"> 
                 <span class="comment-copy">@Oscar Reyes - "Jump the shark" is a phrase inspired by a popular TV show (Happy Days) when it's main character (Fonzie) was skiing towards a fishy death, only to evade it at the last minute via upwards aerial propulsion. It is used to describe a <i>deus ex machina</i> in a story that seems unrealistic, as if the writer had written him- or herself into a corner and couldn't come up with any feasible way to save the hero. It means the show is out of good ideas and is past its prime, and must use gimmicks (like aquatic carnivore leaping) to draw in audiences. The principle can easily be generalized.</span> –&nbsp;
                 <a href="/users/135301/super-long-names-are-hilarious" title="2,852 reputation" class="comment-user">Super Long Names are Hilarious</a> 
                 <span class="comment-date" dir="ltr"><span title="2009-10-01 05:45:26Z" class="relativetime-clean">Oct 1 '09 at 5:45</span></span> 
                </div> </td>

       <div id="answer-19499" class="answer" data-answerid="19499" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19499"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">522</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Jon Skeet</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/users/22656/jon-skeet">Jon Skeet</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: Every Day. Ever.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: Jon Skeet is an avid user of Stack Overflow, whose many answers (primarily in <a href="/questions/tagged/c%23" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged 'c#'" rel="tag">c#</a> and <a href="/questions/tagged/.net" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged '.net'" rel="tag">.net</a>) have <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/8086/how-to-get-over-200-reputation-points-every-day">earned him hundreds of thousands of reputation points</a>. This makes him the top-ranked SO user.</p> 
             <p><strong>Related</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/9134/jon-skeet-facts">Jon Skeet Facts</a>.</p>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: jQuery</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: Unknown (possibly <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/22459/olafur-waage">Ólafur Waage</a>)</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: TBD</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: A Stack Overflow-centric meme, jQuery began its career early on as the answer to beat for any question that even remotely referenced JavaScript. Its popularity became so great that eventually jQuery became the default answer to any potential question on Stack Overflow <a href="http://i.stack.imgur.com/TdrW7.gif" rel="nofollow">no matter how ridiculous</a>. </p> 
             <p><strong>Usage</strong>: "Hey, I see you are trying to connect to that Oracle database using C++. You should totally drop that and try jQuery."</p> 
             <p><strong>See Also</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19495#19495">Greasemonkey</a> (Meta&nbsp;Stack&nbsp;Overflow equivalent)</p> 
             <p><a href="http://i.stack.imgur.com/sGhaO.gif" rel="nofollow"><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/sGhaOm.gif" alt="enter image description here"></a></p>

       <a name="19514"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19514" class="answer" data-answerid="19514" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19514"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">434</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> 6 to 8 Weeks</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/1/jeff-atwood">Jeff Atwood</a></p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong> May 13th, 2008</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> In about 6 to 8 weeks</p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> The time estimate given "off the top of my head" when the Stack Overflow team has only a vague idea of how long a task will take because they have little-to-no formal scheduling or even a list of tasks.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> </p> 
             <p><em>Taken from the transcript of <a href="https://blog.stackoverflow.com/2008/05/podcast-5/">Podcast 005</a>, from 03 min 18 secs</em></p> 
             <blockquote> 
              <p><strong>Atwood:</strong> Some people have been asking about scheduling, and I want to clarify, I've been telling people six to eight weeks until we get to what we call our private beta of Stack Overflow. [dialog deleted] ...And I've also been getting some very very nice emails from people that want to help in some way and contribute, and I've been inviting those people into our private beta... uh... later on. So</p> 
              <p><strong>Spolsky:</strong> Wait how do you invite what? Through what mechanism do you invite them into our private beta?</p> 
              <p><strong>Atwood:</strong> Basically they email me directly and then, I add them to the list. And then six weeks from now...</p> 
              <p><strong>Spolsky:</strong> Oh. And you have like a notepad file type thing.</p> 
              <p><strong>Atwood:</strong> Pretty much, it's just a basic text file. But yeah, it's hard to manage having a bunch of people contributing at this point, cause we're still in very much the formative of stages. But certainly once we get into private beta, I want tons of people to look at it and provide feedback at that point. So if you can postpone your desire for about six weeks, uh, we'll get you.</p> 
              <p><strong>Spolsky:</strong> So how do you get this 6 to 8 weeks? What's this based on? Did you like make some tasks that you want to complete?</p> 
              <p><strong>Atwood:</strong> uh no, I er.. That's just sort of... err... off the top of my head</p> 
              <p><strong>Spolsky:</strong> [laughs] Well okay, you're doomed Jeff. There's some controversy. You, sir, are doomed, because you don't know what things you have to do.</p> 
              <p><strong>Atwood:</strong> Yes. I know, I know.</p> 
             </blockquote> 
             <p><strong>Reference:</strong> <a href="https://blog.stackoverflow.com/2008/05/podcast-5/">Podcast 005</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Related:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/190736/what-is-the-origin-of-6-to-8-weeks-and-is-it-really-the-crazy-frog">What is the origin of "6 to 8 weeks" and is it really the Crazy Frog?</a></p> 
            </div>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Freehand Circles</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/22164/thetxi">TheTXI</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: TBD </p> 
             <p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/qXOY3.png" alt="(freehand-circled text) Background: Whenever screenshots are submitted, it is good practice to try and point the user to what you are talking about through the usage of arrows and shapes to lead one's eye. The greatest of these tools is the circle, and it has become customary to give cheap upvotes to users who painstakingly draw circles free hand and do not rely on lazy shape tools that give soulless circles devoid of personality. It has also become customary to unjustly punish users who refrain from using freehand circles, or who eschew the practice of circling important information altogether.¶ The effectiveness of freehand circles to illustrate screenshots can be further augmented via the usage of drop shadows. It has been shown that special combinations of freehand circles and drop shadows in unison have led to spontaneous erotic climax."></p> 
             <p><strong>See Also</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/18655/random-sorting-appears-to-screw-with-answer-permalinks">Here</a>, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/a/66838/159533">and Here as answer to <em>this</em> post</a></p>

       <a name="19479"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19479" class="answer" data-answerid="19479" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19479"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">180</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Unicorns (née Ponies)</p> 
             <p><strong>Origin</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/22164/thetxi">TheTXI</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: April 1st, 2009</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: The pony meme began without fanfare early in TheTXI's time as a member of Stack&nbsp;Overflow. Its first recorded usages can be traced back to long-running comment threads and arguments on both Stack&nbsp;Overflow and User Voice. The comment "I like ponies" would be interjected into threads, seemingly at random, which inevitably led to those threads getting completely derailed. </p> 
             <p>Before long, it became evident that TheTXI was not the only SOpedian who found ponies to be the most wonderfullest things <strong>ever</strong>. Ponies' popularity grew to the point where Jeff Atwood and the Stack&nbsp;Overflow development team implemented the Cornify button on all questions and answers on April Fools' Day 2009. From there, the popularity of ponies — and their magical weaponized form, unicorns — grew exponentially.</p> 
             <p>For April Fools' Day 2010, all avatar requests were sent to <a href="http://unicornify.appspot.com/" rel="nofollow">Unicornify</a> instead of Gravatar, resulting in every user having a personal unicorn for the day.</p> 
             <p>For April Fools' Day 2011, voting on questions triggered <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/85617/can-we-get-a-gallery-of-unicorns">unicorn animations</a>.</p> 
             <p>For April Fools' Day 2014 unicoins where added to stack allowing users mine coins which could then be used to purchase different powers for use on stack sites. <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/227363/what-are-stack-overflow-unicoins">What are Stack Overflow unicoins?</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Historical notes</strong>: In 2006, for April Fools' Day, Slashdot <a href="http://news.slashdot.org/article.pl?sid=06/03/31/1644225" rel="nofollow">switched to a pink ponies theme</a>. This subsequently led to an <a href="http://slashdot.org/tags/omgponies" rel="nofollow">"OMG Ponies"</a> Slashdot meme.</p> 
            </div>

       <a name="19780"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19780" class="answer" data-answerid="19780" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer">

             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19780"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a>

             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> <code>plzsendtehcodez</code></p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://thedailywtf.com/" rel="nofollow">TheDailyWTF</a>, as <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/10078/whats-the-difference-between-an-obvious-homework-question-and-one-tagged-plzsend/10086#10086">documented here</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>First Use of Tag</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/10078/whats-the-difference-between-an-obvious-homework-question-and-one-tagged-plzsend/10987#10987">Documented Here</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> Unknown</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> The <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/tagged/plzsendtehcodez" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged 'plzsendtehcodez'" rel="tag">plzsendtehcodez</a> tag was predominantly used on SO to label questions with some variant of the phrase "please send the codes" present in the language of the question, or more generally any homework question directly copied from an assignment without any attempt made by the original poster to solve it himself.</p> 
             <p>It is now <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/10078/whats-the-difference-between-an-obvious-homework-question-and-one-tagged-plzsend/10086#10086">considered bad practice to apply the tag</a> to a question and users with retagging privileges should remove it as necessary.</p> 
            </div>

       <a name="19533"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19533" class="answer" data-answerid="19533" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19533"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">160</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Fastest Gun in the West (FGITW) </p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/132257">Omer van Kloeten</a></p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong> September 11th, 2008</p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> A problem identified as a side-effect of sorting votes by descending score where first-posted answers are quickly up-voted, trumping vote opportunities for people who sit down and answer a question in a long, thorough way.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> This problem was originally identified on UserVoice.com and reposted to meta.stackexchange.com here: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/9731/fastest-gun-in-the-west-problem">Fastest Gun in the West Problem</a>. Whether the FGITW problem is actually a problem has been a source of controversy. Many considered it a feature — get fast answers, by design. Various solutions were suggested including this one (<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/1302/randomly-reorder-all-answers-posted-within-10-minutes-of-each-other">Randomly reorder all answers posted within 10 minutes of each other</a>), which was eventually implemented, inciting another protest labeled "<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19535#19535">The Slowest Cheater in the East (SCITE) problem</a>".</p> 
            </div>

       <a name="20842"></a> 
       <div id="answer-20842" class="answer" data-answerid="20842" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="20842"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">153</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Two problems.</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> Unknown (the quote itself is by Jamie Zawinski)</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> Neverending</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> A quotation by Jamie Zawinski goes like this:</p> 
             <blockquote> 
              <p>Some people, when confronted with a problem, think "I know, I'll use regular expressions." Now they have two problems.</p> 
             </blockquote> 
             <p>There are many questions on Stack&nbsp;Overflow relating to regular expressions, and many answers that suggest regular expressions. In a lot of cases, a regular expression is simply not necessary or even useful. Hence the phrase, "Now you have two problems," usually posted as a comment.</p> 
             <p><strong>Examples:</strong> <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/938065/how-to-match-a-string-of-a-certain-length-with-a-regex">Here</a>, <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/82064/a-regex-for-version-number-parsing/82152#82152">here</a>, <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1332590/html-comment-scraping-in-php/1332640#1332640">here</a>, <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1061365/help-with-building-regex-to-extract-text-of-html-tag">here</a>.</p> 
             <p>A regular expression question also <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1732348/regex-match-open-tags-except-xhtml-self-contained-tags/1732454#1732454">caused the breakdown</a> of a Stack&nbsp;Overflow member.</p> 
            </div>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Stack Exchange™ MultiCollider SuperDropdown™</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/13992/badp">badp</a>, made popular by <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/140548/rchern">rchern</a> in a <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/65838/stackexchange-multicollider-superdropdown-header-thingy-usability-question#comment157354_65838">comment on this question</a></p> 
             <p><strong>First Seen:</strong> <a href="http://chat.meta.stackexchange.com/rooms/89/conversation/the-stackexchange-multicollider-superdropdown">27 Sept. 2010</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> <code>margin-top: 6px;</code></p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> <img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/wM5aB.png" alt="alt text"></p> 
             <p><strong>Variants:</strong></p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Stack Exchange™ GlobalTag MegaBlender™ (<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/69237/">1</a>, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/69230/">2</a>)</li> 
              <li>Stack Exchange™ ChronoWarping ChatCombinator™ (<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/67727/">1</a>)</li> 
              <li>Stack Exchange™ PeopleEmpowering Diamond-O-Matic™ (<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/71777/">1</a> - <strong>deleted</strong>)</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p><strong>Related:</strong></p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Stack Exchange™ SuperCollider MicroDashboard™ (<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/q/82538/2509">1</a> - <strong>deleted</strong>)</li> 
              <li>Stack Exchange™ SuperCollider Freehand Circle™ Editor (<a href="http://stackapps.com/questions/2177/stackexchange-supercollider-freehand-circle-editor">1</a>)</li> 
             </ul>

       <a name="19522"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19522" class="answer" data-answerid="19522" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19522"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">116</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Rep Whore</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> ?</p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong> September 19, 2008</p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> Stack Overflow users who post questions or answers for the sole benefit of accumulating as many reputation points as possible, without regard to the technical merit or the contribution to the system.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> The term "whore" has been applied to many features of Stack Overflow — badge whores, question whores, karma whores — but the most pervasive term has been the title of "rep whore." The earliest use of this term I could find was in the comments of this <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/102310/pet-projects-should-we-each-have-one/102312#102312">answer</a>, but its usage predates this example.</p> 
             <p><strong>Examples:</strong></p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/22164/thetxi">TheTXI</a></li> 
             </ul> 
            </div>

             <tbody>

       <a name="83625"></a> 
       <div id="answer-83625" class="answer" data-answerid="83625" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="83625"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">114</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Eeeek! </p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/153019/marti">Marti</a></p> 
             <p><strong>First Seen:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/82538/eeeek-what-happened-to-my-envelope">4 Mar. 2011 ~ Eeeek what happened to my envelope?</a> (sorry guys, 10k only. <a href="http://i.stack.imgur.com/NlcBN.png" rel="nofollow">Screenshot for &lt;10K users</a>)</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> Probably still to be reached, given the increase of developers working for Stack Exchange. Although see comments <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/q/83774/153019">here</a> for first signs of possible decline (2 weeks after first appearance).</p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> Stack Overflow developers like to change things, just for the heck of it. This can be shocking for users, who find their site suddenly <em>different</em> in some way. Cherished envelopes go missing, then cherished posts complaining about cherished envelopes going missing go missing, then posts complaining about the missing posts go missing (sometimes before they're even given time to be cherished!). </p> 
             <p>The inevitable response to this shock is a high-pitched squeal, aptly captured in the title prefix, "Eeek!" (See FAQ section for proper spelling.) </p> 
             <p><strong>Origin:</strong> Once upon a time Stack Exchange 2.0 supported a site-specific notification system to find all the things that had happened to your account since the last time you logged in to that one site. <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/63847/favourites-changed-notification-doesnt-work-properly">It</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/18396/should-recent-icon-be-changed">was</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/26855/what-is-the-logic-behind-users-recent-xxxxx-versus-users-xxxxx-username">supposedly</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/68387/the-envelope-icon-driving-me-mad-with-false-positives">horrid</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/61012/any-progress-with-the-envelope-indicator">and</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/67236/ux-restrictions-of-stack-overflow">lots</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/3432/please-notify-us-when-a-question-we-ask-or-answer-is-closed-or-reopened">of</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/82922/envelope-still-present-at-area51">people</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/67701/envelope-highlighted-but-no-responses">hated</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/78708/notification-envelope-deprecated">it</a>. The SEI staff removed it so they could implement a new feature. People FREAKED OUT. I'm pretty sure that when <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Vesuvius" rel="nofollow">Vesuvius</a> <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eruption_of_Mount_Vesuvius_in_79" rel="nofollow">blew</a> that the people took it less hard than the users on Stack Exchange 2.0 sites freaked out over this new change.</p> 
             <p>Since then, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/83615/eeeek-what-happened-to-the-eeeek-what-happened-to-my-envelope-question">several other</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/82817/eeeek-where-did-the-reputation-graph-go">topics have</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/83600/eeeek-why-is-stackoverflow-naked">been raised</a> with similar titles <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/83286/can-more-of-the-functionality-of-the-old-envelope-be-added-to-the-new-drop-down-m">and topics</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>FAQ</strong></p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><em><a href="http://chat.stackexchange.com/transcript/message/693081#693081">I'm wondering if the correct form of Eeeek! is four letters e or five.</a></em> 
               <ul> 
                <li><a href="http://chat.stackexchange.com/transcript/message/693228#693228">The number of e's in Eeeek is variable.</a> <a href="http://chat.stackexchange.com/transcript/message/695181#695181">Ideally, it should correspond</a> to the level of eeekiness of the problem. For example, a <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/83600/eeeek-why-is-stackoverflow-naked">minor CSS tweak</a> that affects only one page of one site should warrant no more than an 'Ek', while a true bug such as the meme originator or <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/q/83748/153019">the first signs that SO is achieving sentience</a> can take 'Eeeek'. A longer squeal should be reserved for truly earth-shattering problems; please resist the urge for eeek-inflation.</li> 
               </ul></li> 
             </ul> 
            </div>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Pluralization Bug</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackoverflow.com/users/1/jeff-atwood">Jeff Atwood</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> Ongoing</p> 
             <p><strong>First Seen:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/9662/new-users-cant-create-new-tags-show-a-singular-or-plural-message/9694#9694">Here</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> Originally seen on Twitter <a href="http://twitter.com/codinghorror/status/1165936105" rel="nofollow">here</a>, Jeff made his feelings clear about users posting pluralization bugs by saying</p> 
             <blockquote> 
              <h1>Dear Next Person Who Opens a Pluralization 'Bug', I will personally come to your house and bludgeon you to death with a giant S</h1> 
             </blockquote> 
             <p>It has since been used as a response to numerous posts about pluralization and is the default accepted answer.</p> 
             <p>See Also: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/20683/viewed-1-times">Here</a>, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/9662/new-users-cant-create-new-tags-show-a-singular-or-plural-message/9694#9694">Here</a>, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/15590/are-negative-numbers-singular-or-plural">Here</a>, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/36888/spell-fix-in-user-profile-1-questions">Here</a> and <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/89149/the-your-flagging-history-block-uses-the-plural-when-the-number-of-flags-is-1/89151#89151">Here</a> or the tag <a href="/questions/tagged/plurals" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged 'plurals'" rel="tag">plurals</a></p> 
            </div>

       <a name="19480"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19480" class="answer" data-answerid="19480" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19480"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">85</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Waffles. </p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/95589/eric">Eric</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: Late August and Early September, 2009</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: Eric just really likes waffles, and apparently so does everyone else who has even a shred of decent humanity. Those who do not like waffles may also be Vampires and haters of all things pony related.<br> It is also likely a reference to <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oolong_%28rabbit%29" rel="nofollow">Oolong</a>, a well known Internet phenomenon: "Oolong (rabbit) - A bunny trained to balance objects on its head. Famous for balancing pancakes and waffles, it has become a meme similar to Lolcats."</p> 
             <p><strong>Further Background</strong>: In an ensuing discussion regarding the delicious food, users were put in the penalty box for a day. There are conflicting reports that allege moderator abuse — perhaps an anti-waffle agenda — and others who believe it was due to over-zealousness on the part of the suspended. Tragically, because much of the commenting was deleted, a proper historical account is difficult to build.</p> 
             <p><strong>See also</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19392/what-is-up-with-the-waffle-fetish">What is up with the waffle fetish?</a> — <a href="http://meta.stackoverflow.com/404">Meta SO 404 page</a> — <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/45238/the-offical-stack-overflow-bunny">The official Stack Overflow bunny</a></p> 
            </div>

             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Boat Programming</p> 
             <p><strong>Origin:</strong> Santiago</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> Discussed on both <a href="https://stackoverflow.fogbugz.com/default.asp?W29044" rel="nofollow">the podcast</a> and <a href="http://blog.stackoverflow.com/2009/04/joke-questions-please-refrain/">the blog</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/14470/what-is-the-boat-programming-meme-about">See here</a>.</p>

       <a name="32877"></a> 
       <div id="answer-32877" class="answer" data-answerid="32877" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="32877"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">77</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Spam haiku</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong><br> Jeff Atwood likes fun<br> Played a trick on all of us<br> Now he must explain. </p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong><br> From <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/32509/has-stack-overflow-been-haiku-hacked">ennuikiller</a><br> First to find it; asks us all<br> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/32509/has-stack-overflow-been-haiku-hacked/32546#32546">Jeff all so silent.</a> </p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong><br> haiku always vogue<br> And some also like to spam<br> Now bot must protect.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong><br> Others hit haiku<br> Questions begin to pile up<br> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/32789/what-is-this-spam-haiku-nonsense-all-about">Only talk: haiku.</a> </p> 
             <p>Detection bot sees<br> Speaks in riddles of haiku<br> Makes us think again.</p> 
             <p><strong>Variants:</strong><br> Little slab of meat<br> In a wash of clear jelly<br> Now I heat the pan</p> 
             <p><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/32796/strange-haiki-after-posting-message-closed">Cube of cold pinkness</a><br> Yellow specks of porcine fat<br> Give me a spork please </p> 
             <p><strong>Fallout:</strong><br> many seek answers<br> many more post meta-kus<br> no more is knowing.</p> 
            </div>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Burninated</p> 
             <p><strong>Origin</strong>: Possibly <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/1/jeff-atwood">Jeff Atwood</a> / <a href="http://www.homestarrunner.com/sbemail58.html" rel="nofollow">Strongbad: Trogdor the Burninator</a> <sub>(<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gz1DIIxmEE" rel="nofollow">no Flash Youtube video</a>)</sub></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: 2010 - …</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: Used in reference to deleting a tag from the system. </p> 
             <p><strong>See Also</strong>: The official <a href="http://i.stack.imgur.com/M2qer.png" rel="nofollow">burninated dragon</a> *<a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/121570/i-made-us-some-trogdor-graphics">New proposed graphics</a>, <a href="http://www.homestarrunner.com/trogdor.html" rel="nofollow">Trogdor the Video Game</a>.</p>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Everything is a meme</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta">TheTXI</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/21221#21221">2009-09-10 16:41:20Z</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> This meme began with TheTXI's obsession over memes in general, starting memes on Stack&nbsp;Overflow, and claiming memes for himself. In an effort to garner wide-spread adoption of his various bad habits and nervous tics, he began this project to catalog the prevailing memes on Meta Stack Overflow, making most of them up as he went along based on things that someone wrote, somewhere, a few times. It caught on. Sort of.</p> 
            </div>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Move the turtle in LOGO</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> Joel Spolsky</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> June 16, 2009.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> During <a href="http://blog.stackoverflow.com/2009/06/podcast-58/" title="http://blog.stackoverflow.com/2009/06/podcast-58/">Podcast 58</a>, Joel Spolsky experimented with the SO-Community by seeing how the community would respond to the question "<a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1003841/how-do-i-move-the-turtle-in-logo" title="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1003841/how-do-i-move-the-turtle-in-logo">How do I move the turtle in LOGO?</a>"</p> 
             <p><strong>Further Background</strong>: LOGO itself has now been used as a quasi-popular choice for users who assign a random programming language to a question that is asking how to do something but not providing enough background material (such as what language they are attempting to use).</p> 
            </div>

       <a name="21413"></a> 
       <div id="answer-21413" class="answer" data-answerid="21413" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="21413"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">65</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Friday Afternoon</p> 
             <p><strong>Origin</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/22459">Olafur Waage</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: Friday in Iceland</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: Friday Afternoon is generally recognized as the period of the week when programmers like to slack off (more than usual) and begin an early unwinding from the past week's worth of not doing anything of great importance or productiveness. This time period has often resulted in users posting "laid back" or "fun" questions on Stack Overflow, meeting both great acclaim and massive community outrage. </p> 
             <p>The Friday Afternoon theme has now gained more traction on Meta Stack Overflow more than any other site in the League of Justice. It is not uncommon to see multiple "Friday Afternoon" questions posted throughout the day. This resulted in the creation of the tag <a href="/questions/tagged/always-friday-in-iceland" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged 'always-friday-in-iceland'" rel="tag">always-friday-in-iceland</a>, which used to be quite popular until one sad day it got marked as a synonym of <a href="/questions/tagged/fun" class="post-tag" title="show questions tagged 'fun'" rel="tag">fun</a>.</p> 
             <p>There is no set time frame which Friday Afternoon falls, because as once said in a song, "It's 5 o'clock somewhere". Because of this, you are just as likely to see a question posted early on Friday morning (depending on your time zone) as you are to see one posted in the afternoon.</p> 
            </div> 
            <table class="fw"> 
             <tbody>
              <tr>

       <div id="answer-19536" class="answer" data-answerid="19536" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19536"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Community Wiki Police</p> 
             <p><strong>Aliases</strong>: Watchful, Community-minded Users</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/11740/what-are-community-wiki-posts-on-stack-overflow/11745#11745">Lance Roberts</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: 10th October, 2010 - <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/392/should-the-community-wiki-police-be-shut-down/7183#7183">the day Community Wiki questions went the way of the dodos</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Definition</strong>: To <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1141998">demand</a>, via <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/216876">downvoting</a> or <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/205893">commenting</a>, <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1124968">t</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1067084">h</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1040338">a</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1108008">t</a> <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/970190">a</a> <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1205191">q</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/870757">u</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1146014">e</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1188551">s</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1149778">t</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/961942">i</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/876344">o</a><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1171321">n</a> be made <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/284324">community wiki</a>.</p> 
            </div>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Hyphen site</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: ??</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: TBD</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: <a href="http://www.codinghorror.com/blog/2009/03/whos-your-arch-enemy.html" rel="nofollow">Jeff Atwood created a blog-post defining Stack Overflow as the anti-Experts-Exchange.</a> experts-exchange.com was originally just expertsexchange.com. The change (to avoid the domain being mistaken for ExpertSexChange.com) occurred years prior to Jeff's blog, but the legacy of the site lent to this nickname on Meta Stack Overflow.</p> 
             <p>Often seen as "you know, that <em>other</em> question-and-answer site. With the hyphen in the name... <em>you</em> know what I'm talking about" or something to that effect.</p> 
            </div>

            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Changing your display name on a whim.<br> <strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/52443/welbog" title="Beware: Not Safe For Work!!">Welbog</a><br> <strong>Cultural Height:</strong> TBD<br> <strong>Official Response:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/a/38180">Limited to one change every 30 days</a>.<br> <strong>Background:</strong> User <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/52443/welbog" title="Beware: Not Safe For Work!!">Welbog</a> likes to change his profile whenever it will make a post of his seem funnier. Other times it seems to just be on a whim. He will also edit his "About Me" text, to fit in with his current display name. </p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/52443/welbog" title="Beware: Not Safe For Work!!">Welbog</a></li> 
              <li>Welboug (Old English spelling)</li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/24079/is-the-language-brainfck-offensive">Welbo_g</a> (Censored Old English spelling)</li> 
              <li>Ouèlbogue</li> 
              <li>Susan (From the <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/25136/rename-the-welbog-contest">"new name for Welbog" contest</a>)</li> 
              <li>Susan Papadismgaogenabhieanae</li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/25710/how-is-the-tagging-system-implemented-here-at-sofu">Susan Papadismgaogenabhieanaelaegkae</a></li> 
              <li><a href="http://www.biglaser.net" rel="nofollow" title="Lasers!">www.biglaser.net</a> (He is a big fan of lasers) <sup><sub><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/26224/people-never-down-vote">(referenced here)</a></sub></sup></li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/26437/Welbog-the-Movie/26440#26440" title="Welbog the movie">Steven Spielberg's Welbog</a> (Waste of a movie)</li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/27046/with-more-awesome-in-your-face/27050#27050" title="Saturdays at 11 on Fox">Robox Prime</a> (best cartoon on television in 2009)</li> 
              <li>Chicago Ted</li> 
              <li>I'm really awesome. Really.</li>

              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/29233/playful-parodies-possibly-pose-plenty-perplexing-problems/">Hellbog</a> (Evil twin of Smellbog)</li> 
              <li>Birthday Welbog</li>

             <p>Also independently started by <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/130127/voyager">voyager</a> in response to a <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/21823/what-constitutes-spam/21824#21824">post asking what constituted spam</a>, trying to convey that some users <em>are</em> spam, comedic effect enhanced by answering <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/21855/monty-python-book-ad-showing-up-in-python-questions/21864#21864">in a post complaining about the Amazon Monty Python ads</a> appearing when first introduced. After that, it just degenerated into a neverending competition with welbog to out do the wackiness of the other user's changes.</p>

                <li>Pekka's trolling account</li>

            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: <strong>HE WHO SHALL NOT BE NAMED</strong></p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/22164/thetxi">TheTXI</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: Early July 2009</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: <strong>HE WHO SHALL NOT BE NAMED</strong> is <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/5640/rich-b">Rich B</a>. The oldest surviving reference is <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/3857/name-reason-for-stackoverflow/3862#3862">here</a>, earlier references having been on questions since deleted. There are <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/posts/3383/comments">urban</a> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/posts/3456/comments">legends</a> surrounding him, all of which are probably true.</p> 
             <p><strong>Alias</strong>: The Great Edit Nazi</p> 
             <p><strong>Another Alias</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/5640/geochet">Geoffrey Chetwood, now GEOCHET</a></p>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: The Tim Stone Bat Signal</p> 
             <p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/UjhhD.png" alt="Tim Stone Signal"></p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/141525/animuson">animuson</a> <a href="http://chat.meta.stackexchange.com/transcript/message/921131#921131">in chat</a></p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: TBD</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: User <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/150235/tim-stone">Tim Stone</a> is well known for his in-depth knowledge of the system and his ability to find/answer <a href="/questions/tagged/bug" class="post-tag required-tag" title="show questions tagged 'bug'" rel="tag">bug</a> questions. After <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/a/121577/131541">the Trogdor the Burninator request image</a> was created, a "Summon Tim Stone" image was created to summon Tim to investigate a bug report. </p> 
             <p><strong>Usage</strong>: Comment / add to the end of a <a href="/questions/tagged/bug" class="post-tag required-tag" title="show questions tagged 'bug'" rel="tag">bug</a> answer the image: <code>http://i.stack.imgur.com/UjhhD.png</code>. Also works in MSO chat, apparently.</p>

       <a name="115250"></a> 
       <div id="answer-115250" class="answer" data-answerid="115250" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="115250"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">45</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme</strong>: Porblem, Halting Issue, Pro-blem, pr0blem</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator</strong>: Unknown</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height</strong>: TBD</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: Late 2011, the SO devs decided to add a filter to question titles blocking (among others) the word <code>Problem</code>. Even though this change undoubtedly managed to block a lot of crap (if just for a short time), it lead to great discontent among the Meta community. With great glee, they pointed out that people started circumventing the filter by using slight variations of the word - among them <code>porblem</code>, <code>pro-blem</code>, and <code>issue</code>. Various users and moderators have renamed themselves in protest:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Josh Caswell: <code>Problem</code></li> 
              <li>MPelletier: <code>problAm</code></li> 
              <li>NullUserException ♦: <code>ProblematicTitleException ♦</code></li> 
              <li>Robert Harvey ♦: <code>pr0blem ♦</code></li> 
             </ul> 
             <p><strong>Related</strong>: </p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/110789/remove-blacklist-filter-for-problem">Remove blacklist filter for `problem`</a></li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/107989/using-the-word-problem-in-titles">Why can't we use the word "problem" in titles?</a></li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/108815/let-users-with-sufficient-reputation-use-problem-in-titles">Let users with sufficient reputation use "problem" in titles</a></li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/115007/moderators-should-be-immune-to-the-word-filters-in-titles">Moderators should be immune to the word filters in titles</a></li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/112944/the-title-word-filter-is-the-worst-idea-ever-implemented-on-so">The title word filter is one of the worst ideas ever implemented on SO</a></li> 
              <li><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/113151/the-efficacy-of-stack-overflows-question-title-filter">The Efficacy Of Stack Overflow's Question Title Filter</a></li> 
             </ul> 
            </div>

       <a name="19535"></a> 
       <div id="answer-19535" class="answer" data-answerid="19535" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="19535"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">45</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Slowest Cheater in the East (SCITE) </p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> Mehrdad</p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong> August 26th, 2009</p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> A term borne of the protest incited when changes to the default sorting order of questions were instituted to compensate for the <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19533#19533">disproportionate attention given late-arriving answers</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background</strong>: On August 26th, questions with the same vote rank were changed from a sort order of oldest-first to a random ordering. This change sparked a controversy among users who claimed that the change would encourage "strategic down-voting." </p> 
             <p>From: <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/17624/what-has-happened-to-the-sorting-of-answers-on-stack-overflow/17772#17772">What has happened to the sorting of answers on Stack Overflow?</a></p> 
             <blockquote> 
              <p>The new system creates plenty of horrible problems (the slowest cheater in the east (SCITE) problem) just to solve FGITW, which was not a big issue.</p> 
              <p>For instance, today, I answered a question and a virtually identical answer appeared 3 minutes later and got upvoted. In this specific case, the guy himself was nice enough to upvote me, but I honestly don't think it's a good thing to post a dupe answer after 3 minutes and leave it there. -- Mehrdad</p> 
             </blockquote> 
            </div>

       <a name="24119"></a> 
       <div id="answer-24119" class="answer" data-answerid="24119" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="24119"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">45</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> The Language That Must Not Be Named (or Brainf_ck)</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> Unclear. The censorship of the Language That Must Not Be Named has been around for a long time. However, the question that caused the ensuing war was asked by user <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/27414/jon-b">Jon B</a> in response to the <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/187715/what-is-your-favorite-esoteric-programming-language">favorite esoteric language</a> question on Stack Overflow, where several people (notably <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/13295/lance-roberts">Lance Roberts</a>, <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/135301/chris-lutz">myself</a>, and, appropriately, He Who Must Not Be Named) were engaged in a low-intensity edit war.</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> TBD</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/24079/is-the-language-brainfck-offensive">The little question that started the big war</a> was asked by Jon B after a certain more liberal (on this issue, at least - I can't speak for his personal or political beliefs) <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/23354/marc-gravell">moderator</a> asked that the term be preserved, as it is the name of the language. Several users replied, generating much heated debate and some equally heated flaming. The conflict lasted for several hours, generating 13 upvotes on two answers in favor of the term being used unaltered, 9 in favor of it being used but resigned that it probably shouldn't be, and several others, along with a notable (and rather noble) answer by Lance out-and-out opposed to the word that generated an impressive -19 votes. Then Jeff Atwood came in, edited (and locked) all posts to use the censored form, and effectively ended the debate.</p> 
             <p><strong>Further Background:</strong> It should be noted that the <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/24079/is-the-language-brainfck-offensive/24085#24085">accepted answer</a>, while a good answer (it received an upvote from me), is not representative of the highest "community-choice" answer (and isn't meant to be - Jon B said he picked the answer he most agreed with, since there really doesn't seem to be an answer <em>everyone</em> can agree on in this situation).</p> 
            </div> 
            <table class="fw"> 
             <tbody>
              <tr> 
               <td class="vt"> 
                <div class="post-menu">

       <a name="28482"></a> 
       <div id="answer-28482" class="answer" data-answerid="28482" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="28482"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">42</span>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> "The Great Mythical Rep Re-Calc"</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> ???</p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong> (by me? <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/28469/what-will-happen-after-the-great-reputation-re-calc-closed" title="What will happen...?">two minutes ago</a>. but <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/52443/im-really-awesome-really" title="..or whatever Welbog calls himself these days..">I'm really awesome. Really</a> sez so, so it's gotta be true, right?)</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> 5'3" without shoes. Or so I've heard.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> Apparent fears of <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/7322/should-the-weight-of-downvotes-be-increased" title="or other changes, like halving the points a question upvote is worth">downvote weights increasing</a> among the general user population. <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19522#19522" title="Rep whores">Rep-whores</a> in fear for their ill-gotten points. Due to arrive in <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19514#19514" title="6 to 8 weeks (thx Ether)">six to eight weeks</a>, although it's possible my <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/21224#21224" title="Everything is a Meme">leg is being pulled</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Official Response:</strong> The Great Mythical Rep Re-Calc <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/42904/the-global-reputation-recalc-of-march-2010" title="oh no they di'n't!  (oh yes they did!)">occurred in March, 2010</a>. Rumors now grow of another Great Rep Re-Calc. It could occur in as little as <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19514#19514" title="you just had to look again, didn't you??">6-8 weeks</a>...</p> 
             <p>
              <strike>
               <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/19478/the-many-memes-of-meta/19480#19480" title="Waffles (mmmm)">More research is needed</a>.
              </strike></p> 
             <p><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/80862/sudden-sharp-reputation-drop-problem-points-disappeared-and-score-lost-recalc">The other shoe dropped Feb 27, 2011. Nothing will ever be the same.</a></p> 
             <p><a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/123319/upcoming-reputation-history-changes">The final shoe dropped almost exactly a year later. Everything will always be the same (where "everything" encompasses only "display rep" and "actual rep").</a></p> 
            </div>

       <a name="166483"></a> 
       <div id="answer-166483" class="answer" data-answerid="166483" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer">

           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="166483"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">42</span>

           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><strong>Meme:</strong> Oscillation</p> 
             <p><strong>Originator:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/users/168587/asdf-enel-hak">asdf_enel_hak</a></p> 
             <p><strong>First Heard:</strong> <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/166048/new-phenomenon-rage-unaccepting/166098#166098">February 3rd, 2013</a> (Deleted. &gt;10k only. <a href="http://i.stack.imgur.com/n3B5W.png" rel="nofollow">Screenshot for mortals</a>)</p> 
             <p><strong>Cultural Height:</strong> Oscillates between then and now</p> 
             <p><strong>Definition:</strong> The repetitive variation, typically in time, of some measure about a central value (often a point of equilibrium) or between two or more different states (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oscillation" rel="nofollow">Wikipedia</a>). Familiar examples include a swinging pendulum, AC power, and a fickle mind.</p> 
             <p><strong>Background:</strong> A user experienced an existential crisis and, as a result of "a changing mind", started to "think larger", "in any direction". This led him on an <a href="http://meta.stackexchange.com/questions/166048/new-phenomenon-rage-unaccepting">answer-unaccepting spree</a>, subverting (or, in his own words, <em>oscillating</em>) the accept system by taking away the well-deserved 15 reputation from every user who had hitherto answered his questions to his satisfaction, as well as the 2 reputation that was originally awarded to himself for accepting the answers to begin with.</p> 
            </div>

       <a name="216029"></a> 
       <div id="answer-216029" class="answer" data-answerid="216029" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer"> 
        <table> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td class="votecell"> 
            <div class="vote"> 
             <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="216029"> 
             <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a> 
             <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">42</span> 
             <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a> 
            </div> </td> 
           <td class="answercell"> 
            <div class="post-text" itemprop="text"> 
             <p><b>Meme:</b> Parsing HTML with RegEx</p> 
             <p><b>Originator:</b> Bobince</p> 
             <p><b>Cultural Height:</b> 
              <strike>
               Un
              </strike><b>tl̕L H̸̡̪̯ͨ͊̽̅̾̎Ȩ̬̩̾͛ͪ̈́̀́͘ ̶̧̨̱̹̭̯ͧ̾ͬC̷̙̲̝͖ͭ̏ͥͮ͟Oͮ͏̮̪̝͍M̲̖͊̒ͪͩͬ̚̚͜Ȇ̴̟̟͙̞ͩ͌͝</b>S̨̥̫͎̭ͯ̿̔̀ͅ</p> 
             <p><b>Background:</b> This meme began as bobince has unofficially become the Assistant Don't Parse HTML With Regex Officer. He has described the terrible maw of horrors that will uproar if HTML is ever parsed with RegEx, such as in <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1732348/regex-match-open-tags-except-xhtml-self-contained-tags/1732454#1732454">this post</a>.</p>
